We annually (at least in late 90s) rented a huge Ryder moving truck and set up a station in there with Cmas lights, couches and other sleeping spaces, TV and VCR, and other comforts that made it more like a fun social event than a first aid stand.  It kind of goes to show the most innocuous appearing event can rapidly turn belly up.", "id": "10151806480247879_28139703", "user_likes": false}, {"from": {"id": "1188435539", "name": "Chris Villar"}, "like_count": 0, "can_remove": false, "created_time": "2013-11-18T16:06:34+0000", "message": "I just posted this to my wall.  I thought current students might appreciate it:\n\n14 years ago today I was 1 semester out of school and my alarm clock radio awoke me to the news of the Bonfire collapse. I flew to my phone to call Angie, who was very involved in Bonfire. She'd left me a chilling voice mail 5 hours earlier. Because of that VM, I knew it was only an accident of fate, but my little sister was safe. Her dorm, FHK, had been on shift and she was a witness. In a daze I went to work for about 5 minutes before I got in the car and drove the 100 miles to College Station where I was still on EMS staff. \n\nAt stack site, I found Angie, gave her a hug and made sure she was holding up. She wasn't but she was glad I was there. I needed to see how I could help. The site was a beehive of activity. The last survivor had been extricated hours before but we didn't know that for sure yet. Under direction of CSFD, trees were being pulled off stack with precision to make sure there was no shifting. Hundreds of students were moving trees away from stack and hundreds more stood by to help if needed. Still thousands more stood by in silent vigil. Everybody's emotions were raw. It was surreal. \n\nMy close college friends, all of whom were medics on EMS or Care Team, had been working all night. I relieved the attendant on 862 and joined the vigil.
